<text>Good Concept, Decent Food
We had lunch at the La Canada branch of this fresh Mediterranean fast casual concept. Although somewhat Americanized, the ingredients were fresh and the food was fine. After ordering at the counter, the food is brought to your table as it is made (not necessarily all at once). The main difference between this place and more traditional places serving similar food is that Luna Grill is more expensive and has less bold flavors. < review>
Chicken is very tasty.  I ordered a seasonal beet salad and added chicken. This is an order at the counter before being seated casual place.  Indo find their combinations a bit odd.  My salad had roasted tomatoes but fairly pedestrian  beets that could have come out of a can, which I love but I guess was expecting something a bit more elevated.  They serve hummus which I am not a big  fan of and do not serve baba ganoush/mouttabal (which I love!).   I tasted my lunch partner's.  It had a strange sweetness and was not that thick.  I realise there are many different cultures represented in Middle-Eastern cooking. Having never eaten at a Halal establishment and my expectations being based on my 50 or so years of  eating Israeli, Persian, Lebanese, and Armenian food probably coloured my perception but all-in-all food was fresh and tasty.  This is a good casual dining option in LA Canada.</review>

English BR

Like a gourmet Habib's that serves healthy food, but infinitely better than a Habib's. But it does not remind Habib's why it has esfiha, but because it is a Middle Eastern food franchise, with several addresses in California and some in Texa.

Everything is very tasty, it is nothing out of this world, but it is a good quick and affordable option, with several dishes common to us Brazilians, such as cigars, falafel, hummus, tabules, very generous salads and the combined dishes, also very well served. without misery.

< review>
Hidden gem!  Don't be fooled by the old dingy sign--this place is high quality with low prices.  Possibly he best fresh-made Chinese buffet-style food in the area!  Combos + a la carte.  Vegetables are crisp, meat is plentiful, servings are absolutely huge, I mean they stuff those take-out containers to capacity.  The orange chicken is crisp, tender + gorgeously flavorful.  Beef with broccoli is very good, Kung Pao chicken is another favorite.  Foodland beats all those chain Chinese places hands-down.  They also have Mexican food which I haven't tried but chances are it's done well because these people can really cook.< /review>

<Time>1619734156601<//Time><Rating>5</Rating><Text>Fast service and friendly! All my tire issues fixed in less than 30 min! Opa!</Text>< Pics>
None</Pics>
< Resp>
None<//Resp>
<gmap_id>0x8085734dec4befd5:0x6118f0a141d97879<//gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<UserId.>103756142999283894215</UserId.>< user_name>
Jaroslaw Syzdek< /user_name>
< time>
1601004460792< /time>
<rating>5</rating>< Review>
I came here twice to install tires, for two different vehicles. One was a lifted pick-up truck with oversized tires, the other one was just a normal car. While most places do small tires fine, they generally can't handle big off-road wheels well, especially in the Bay Area where most people drive smaller vehicles. These guys did a fine job on both vehicles. The truck took about an hour (I was also replacing the spare tire, so that's 5 wheels), the car was about half an hour. They have a spacious seating area and I was able to make myself coffee, pull out my laptop and just do some work while they were taking care of the wheels. I really admire how well they did with the truck. Those are some big tires and there is absolutely no vibration or anything. I drove there from Oakland and it was worth it.
BTW, while I was waiting, I could see how they treat their customers: both in person and over the phone. They were professional, honest, no BS. Highly recommend this place.</Review>

<UserId.>106662344045469412664< /UserId.><gmapID>0x80dc9b0de03f4dc3:0x5ffe018cfc0e8559<//gmapID>< Review>
I signed up for Skydive Elsinore's "Accelerated Freefall Level 1" in part because I'm terrified of heights, and in part because my friend was and I didn't want him to go alone.  (AFF means you jump with an instructor on either side, but you are jumping yourself, controlling yourself, and land your own parachute, vs a tandem jump where the instructor is strapped to you and can handle any aspects of the jump you don't want to)

The campus is cool.  There's definitely a "bro" vibe, but it's not overpowering. Everyone is super friendly and excited.  Everyone is willing to answer questions and wants to help, from instructors to random jumpers.

Once you get into classroom, the facility gets very professional and it reminded me of a more intimate, more friendly Army classroom.

The instructors were patient and detail oriented.  We drilled a LOT on the ground, including how to handle every conceivable type of emergency, with a lot of visual aids and exercises which left me confident I could get safely to ground no matter what happened. We even practiced exit procedures from what I think may have been the real tail sections of decommissioned planes.

The aircraft I went up in felt very new (and even had modern avionics, which I was not expecting at all)

In the air, even though I had poor body position the instructors kept me on track and were re-assuring, friendly, supportive and professional.

The landing pattern which seemed scary and narrow when I was on the ground looking at maps was super easy to navigate from the air and landing, just like all the in-air exercises were very easy because the instructors had taken their time to drill the process over and over on the ground.

I can not think of a single complaint. I am over the moon happy with Skydive Elsinore and give them an unqualified recommendation.< /Review>

<text>I am from London and was recently on a California road trip wherein I decided to finally check Tandem Skydiving off my bucket list! Elsinore is a great place visually and I thought the pricing was just right too. When I got there, the staff and the friendly instructors there made me feel extremely comfortable. For anyone who's thinking of doing a Tandem jump here, I can assure you that it's worth it. The instructors here jump like 15-20 times a day, and are alive n fit! So you can be sure that they know what they are doing, their equipment doesn't fail, and they will try their best to ensure that it goes well for you. I bought the Pro package which ensured that a recording instructor flies with me. The recording instructors also do a fantastic job. They cover the whole thing as a story. So you have a full story at the end, and can re-live the moments later. I had a problem loading my video later, but they sorted me out in no time. <text>Skydiving was probably one of the BEST things i've ever done in my entire life! I came here to celebrate my friends 21st birthday and after two weeks of contemplating this once in a lifetime opportunity to skydive I probably would have never thought of actually going haha!!. It was a group of us and our appointment was set at 11 A.M. however, the sky was very cloudy that day so therefore we had to wait a couple of hours to see if the clouds would clear up. I was very optimistic that we were gonna skydive that day ! Shout out to the guy we met there named Stake! He gave us a tour around the grounds (only because it was very cloudy and it was a high chance that we weren't going to be able to skydive due to weather). He showed us the airplanes and just told us what to expect when we were going to jump hahaha! After a couple hours of waiting the sun began to come out and the clouds started to clear up and it was showtime !! Justin (super funny dude) was my skydive instructor and I cannot thank him enough for making my first skydive experience so much fun! He kept ensuring me that everything was gonna go smooth and he was very knowledgeable about skydiving and he told me everything I have to do to make this go well. Honestly I wasn't as nervous as I was days before but I was just so ready to experience this thrill! Justin made sure that I was secure and as soon as we were getting ready to get on the plane, he told me that we were going first haha. I was jumping at Skydive Elsinore in November/December..

< review>
This was my first time skydiving. I'd heard before that skydiving is a "hurry up and wait" kind of experience, so I was prepared for it. I made my appointment for 11/2 at 9 am, but I showed up at 8:30. (It's just always better to have the extra cushion of time.) What you need to understand first off is that your safety is in their hands, and they have a lot of factors to contend with - wind/weather conditions, properly securing the equipment, seeing to every jumper, and yes, the paperwork, because if you haven't heard, Americans are kind of litigious, and they have to cover their bases. So you likely won't be going up right on time. I, myself didn't get geared up until closer to 10, but hey, if that's the cost of me safely landing from a 12,500 foot drop, then that's fine by me!
I was lucky to get Marcelo as my instructor - he immediately made me feel right at ease with everything. He was very friendly, personable, and positive. Even with the plane at the full altitude, I wasn't anxious like I thought I would be. And the jump? Well, you'd just have to try it for yourself to know what it's really like! In Elsinore, you see it all - the desert, the mountains, and the sea. It was an incredible experience, and I will definitely be doing it again. I am so glad I came here for my first jump!</review>

<Date>1541385763339<//Date>< Review>
It was my Dads 60th so we got him a skydiving trip, my wife and a close family friend all went with him.  The original day we went was too cloudy we had to reschedule , which was a breeze to do with the very friendly and helpful staff. Today we went and the staff was great very social and really pumped it up to make it fun, I have to say that Jared was a shining star and just his energy made me want to sign up, but then I realized I was a chicken. we did the video package everything was great, our good friend had a rough landing where she didn't get her feet up and it looks like she broke her ankle. Again the staff were very good professional and caring but I think they need to improve the communication with the family on when an incident happens, however seldom it may be. The instructors did a great job getting her the care she needed , I hope that the instructor H. doesn't blame himself. the video and pictures are well worth the money because it is such a whirlwind of a trip, its good to look back on.  all in all I would recommend going skydiving her and strongly recommend you practice lifting your legs up before you go!</Review>

<UserId.>117445242916250850775<//UserId.>< name>
Alexander Greene< /name>
< date>
1542255540074< /date>
<rating>3< /rating>< text>
Skydive Elsinore provides a very unique experience for those willing to be hurled out of an aircraft and into a freefall. Their staff are well qualified, and know what they are doing.

From a critical perspective, it appears that scheduling could be managed a little better. Our early morning schedule which was purchased in advance was delayed and we, along with other tandem jumpers waited approximately 5 hours before the jump. The wait was not due to weather, or mechanical delays, as group after group went ahead. When inquiring about the status of the assigned jump the typical answer given was "about thirty more minutes" which degraded into uncertainty.

It could be that this situation was rare.

Overall, you'll enjoy the experience, but be prepared to wait just in case it turns into an unexpectedly long day.</text>

<Pictures>None< /Pictures>< review>
Easy process. Nice people. Lots of fun. I took my son for his 18th birthday. He was not feeling well and we got through the whole process waiting to get on the plane. He wanted to jump do badly I could not convince him to come back another day until his headache was so bad he decided to reschedule. Lake Elsinore Skydiving made it super easy to reschedule.  I just called them up when we were ready a few weeks later and we showed up. The instructors were nice. Only issue is waiting around not knowing how long is going to take to get to from start to finish. They tell you it would be a two to four hour process. That kind of kills your day and any plans. Lots of fun nonetheless. My son had an awesome time. My ears started hurting super bad with the altitude change on the freefall. They're still plugged up. Another young man in the plane said the same thing when we were finishing up. Not sure how to change that or what to recommend for someone else, just know there's a possibility this may occur.</review>

< Text>
I'm an AFF student and had my first jumps yesterday.

Ground coach: Lindsay
AFF Level 1: Luca & Brodie
AFF Level 2: Luca & Cory

First off the staff are all AMAZING people. Fun, enjoyable, and super professional when it comes to "safety" and training.

I trust my life with these individuals and have complete confidence in their skills and abilities simply because of the fact that they know what the hell they are doing and have the jumps to prove it.

The facility is pretty nice and I really liked the metal work throughout the entire place. There's a stainless steel logo in the office and the welds blew my mind. Clean bathrooms and showers. Nice shaded area to chill.

***ADVICE FOR AFF LEVEL 1 STUDENTS***
PLAN AHEAD ON STAYING 2 DAYS just in case.

Personally, as a student, I think it's better to make a weekend out of it whenever you visit Skydive Elsinore. There's a lot to learn and trying learn anything after a 2 hour commute is daunting.

This isn't like getting a Bachelor's Degree. There's no "pass and forget" so make sure you are fresh and ready soak in the important info and be ready to drill it in! 100% commitment.

In retrospect, I thought it was a more beneficial to the learning process to have the ground class, sleep on it, study, and be rested and alert for the next day.

Lastly, after everything is checked and rechecked, the wind still determines who jumps. The entire facility can be grounded if the weather is bad.

Levels 2-8 do not take that long and neither do the solos. You can easily get multiple jumps completed in 1 day; however, staying that extra day and keeping a track of the weather before you go will maximize your chances of getting your jumps in.

Do not schedule things too far in advance because the weather can change. You have to be flexible.

One thing not listed on their website is that they offer wind tunnel training with a coach. If you are between Levels 3 and 4 it is a great option to explore< /Text>
